  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_949f0976-fee9-415d-931a-04b72b8560c8'
      });

<span id="freeTextContainer14856524402049626485">While the Titanic and Lusitania are both well-documented disasters, the single greatest tragedy in maritime history is the little-known January 30, 1945 sinking in the Baltic Sea by a Soviet submarine of the Wilhelm Gustloff, a German cruise liner that was supposed to ferry wartime personnel and refugees to safety from the advancing Red Army. The ship was overcrowded with </span>
  <span id="freeText14856524402049626485" style="display:none">While the Titanic and Lusitania are both well-documented disasters, the single greatest tragedy in maritime history is the little-known January 30, 1945 sinking in the Baltic Sea by a Soviet submarine of the Wilhelm Gustloff, a German cruise liner that was supposed to ferry wartime personnel and refugees to safety from the advancing Red Army. The ship was overcrowded with more than 10,500 passengers — the intended capacity was approximately 1,800 — and more than 9,000 people, including 5,000 children, lost their lives. <br /><br />Sepetys (writer of 'Between Shades of Gray') crafts four fictionalized but historically accurate voices to convey the real-life tragedy. Joana, a Lithuanian with nursing experience; Florian, a Prussian soldier fleeing the Nazis with stolen treasure; and Emilia, a Polish girl close to the end of her pregnancy, converge on their escape journeys as Russian troops advance; each will eventually meet Albert, a Nazi peon with delusions of grandeur, assigned to the Gustloff decks.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14856524402049626485" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      </div>

<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/47021662-g"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1491864386i/47021662._UX100_CR0,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/47021662-g">G</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<div class='spoiler'>
This answer contains spoilers…
<span class='spoilerAnswerText'>
<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  
    The person is Clara Christensen.<br />Clara Christensen is a woman who lives with her husband on the coast near the sinking site of the Wilhelm Gustloff. Th<a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">…more</a>
    The person is Clara Christensen.<br />Clara Christensen is a woman who lives with her husband on the coast near the sinking site of the Wilhelm Gustloff. They were the ones who found Emilia's body, but they never knew who she was. <br />At the time of the letter, Clara had a news article about Halinka (Emilia's daughter), who wanted to be an Olympic swimmer for the US. However, because she was born on a ship, her nationality was questioned.<br />Long story short, after reading the article, Clara realized that Emilia was Halinka's mother, and wrote to Florian about it, who had adopted Halinka and Klaus with Joana.<a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">(less)</a>
  
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>
</span>
</div>
</span>

          }
        });
      });

</script>    </div>

<div id="review_1438243273" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1438243273" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1438243273?book_show_action=true">Nov 09, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2016">2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=arc">arc</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1438243273" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5994958207744647585">I try, I really do, but <b>Sepetys's war stories do nothing for me</b>. Yes, I know I'm in the minority. I was one of few who didn't love her debut - <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7824322.Between_Shades_of_Gray' title='Between Shades of Gray by Ruta Sepetys' rel='nofollow noopener'>Between Shades of Gray</a> - and much preferred her second book - <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11178225.Out_of_the_Easy' title='Out of the Easy by Ruta Sepetys' rel='nofollow noopener'>Out of the Easy</a>. Now she returns to World War II and, once again, I don't get it.<br/><br/>As with her first novel, I feel a little uncomfortable being negative about these kinds of books. This was a horrific time when some terrible atrocities were committed and I applaud the author for always focusing o</span>
  <span id="freeText5994958207744647585" style="display:none">I try, I really do, but <b>Sepetys's war stories do nothing for me</b>. Yes, I know I'm in the minority. I was one of few who didn't love her debut - <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7824322.Between_Shades_of_Gray" title="Between Shades of Gray by Ruta Sepetys" rel="nofollow noopener">Between Shades of Gray</a> - and much preferred her second book - <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11178225.Out_of_the_Easy" title="Out of the Easy by Ruta Sepetys" rel="nofollow noopener">Out of the Easy</a>. Now she returns to World War II and, once again, I don't get it.<br /><br />As with her first novel, I feel a little uncomfortable being negative about these kinds of books. This was a horrific time when some terrible atrocities were committed and I applaud the author for always focusing on the unknown, but no less true, parts of history. <br /><br />Many of us know the tales of German and Polish Jews during the Nazi reign, far less know what Lithuanian refugees faced. Even fewer will know of the tragedy this book is about. I like that. Historical fiction that teaches me something is always appreciated. However, a few history lessons is truly all I took from this book.<br /><br />The story is told in very short chapters of 2-3 pages (sometimes just a few sentences) and the perspective jumps between four different people - Joana, Florian, Emilia and Alfred. Personally, this didn't work for me. We spent so little time with each character before moving on that I constantly felt distanced from them, never making an emotional connection. In the beginning, the rapid movement between perspectives even made it difficult to follow the story.<br /><br />Sepetys, for me, writes <b>some of the most detached accounts of WW2 atrocities</b>. It honestly shouldn't be that hard to evoke sympathy or some feeling for these poor people, but I genuinely felt nothing. You know those expendable people that get gunned down in movies while the hero runs from the bad guys? The ones who the camera brushes over and we never think about again? That is how I felt when learning of all the casualties and brutality in this book.<br /><br />The book is told in one long, tedious journey and features many flashbacks that failed to pique my interest. The present is literally about them trekking across the icy landscape and having to show their papers to one soldier after another, before finally getting to the boat they want to board. I'm sorry, but <b>it was so boring</b>.<br /><br />Maybe I could put it down to recently reading a fast-paced, exciting (and horrifying) book set during the Second World War - <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18743370.Front_Lines__Soldier_Girl___1_" title="Front Lines (Soldier Girl, #1) by Michael Grant" rel="nofollow noopener">Front Lines</a> - but, to be honest, I just think the author's war stories are not for me. I'm an emotional reader, and this kind of narrative leaves me cold.<br /><br /><a href="http://thebookgeek.org" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/thebookgeekreviews" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/thebookgeek01" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://instagram.com/emleemay" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/EmilyMayTheBookGeek" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a href="https://society6.com/bookgeek/" rel="nofollow noopener">Store</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="5994958207744647585" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1456890925" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1456890925" />
    <a title="Maggie Stiefvater" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1246837-maggie-stiefvater"><img alt="Maggie Stiefvater" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1587234846p2/1246837.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1456890925?book_show_action=true">Dec 01, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maggie Stiefvater" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maggie Stiefvater" href="/user/show/1246837-maggie-stiefvater">Maggie Stiefvater</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1246837-maggie-stiefvater?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1246837-maggie-stiefvater?shelf=recommended">recommended</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1456890925" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12443716971349948975">This swift-footed, kind-hearted historical is intensely satisfying in just about all the ways a novel can be satisfying. Without further ado, here are five things you should know about it before picking it up:<br/><br/>1. A lot of times, historical fiction shows its work. As a history major, I don't mind a research-filled brick of a book, but I'd think carefully about who I recommended it to. Historical can be dense. Salt to the Sea is not that book: Sepetys chooses her word battles carefully for an incre</span>
  <span id="freeText12443716971349948975" style="display:none">This swift-footed, kind-hearted historical is intensely satisfying in just about all the ways a novel can be satisfying. Without further ado, here are five things you should know about it before picking it up:<br /><br />1. A lot of times, historical fiction shows its work. As a history major, I don't mind a research-filled brick of a book, but I'd think carefully about who I recommended it to. Historical can be dense. Salt to the Sea is not that book: Sepetys chooses her word battles carefully for an incredibly fast read. Short chapters elbow you and say "read just one more, right?" until the book is all gone.<br /><br />2. I wanted to call this a thriller when I first started typing up this recommendation, but the term's not quite right. It's quite fast-paced, but THRILLER feels wrong: it's not quite got that frantic electricity. ADVENTURE is closer, but still wrong. Shouldn't there be jeeps and a comic relief side kick in an adventure? There's mostly just soldiers and frostbite and abandoned soup in this one, which is not the same. Nevertheless, you should know: it's not a depressing book, although sad things happen in it.<br /><br />3. The characters are lovely. There are many of them, all deftly and lightly-drawn, and because they come from all ages and backgrounds, the dynamics between them are ever-changing. It's told from four points of view to allow the reader to spin around the story from all angles, and because each of the POV characters brings something very different to the table, this swapping of eyes is satisfying rather than frustrating. <br /><br />4. Sepetys has two other historicals out that I enjoyed a lot, but this one has headed briskly to the top of the list. it's confident and stylish in a way that is really satisfying to see.<br /><br />5. This novel is the natural successor to Code Name Verity: a character-driven, accessible, YA historical with all the feels you could desire and enough research to bring down an elephant. If elephants were brought down by research.<br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12443716971349948975" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1899564117" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1899564117" />
    <a title="Cristina Monica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica"><img alt="Cristina Monica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589617514p2/14596170.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1899564117?book_show_action=true">Feb 01, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cristina Monica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cristina Monica" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica">Cristina Monica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=world-war-ii">world-war-ii</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1899564117" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13295872412830525123">4.5 stars.<br/><br/>No wonder SALT TO THE SEA won the 2016 Goodreads Choice Award for Young Adult Fiction. It’s pretty darn captivating. <br/><br/>Every time I finish reading an historical novel, especially the WWII ones, I find the need to congratulate myself. It’s no secret that those novels are usually heavy in emotions and historical elements.<br/><br/>Yet Ruta Sepetys made reading this YA historical novel so easy. I didn’t even feel the necessity to take a dozen breaks between chapters. And that’s because it’s so…<br/><br/>Access</span>
  <span id="freeText13295872412830525123" style="display:none">4.5 stars.<br /><br />No wonder SALT TO THE SEA won the 2016 Goodreads Choice Award for Young Adult Fiction. It’s pretty darn captivating. <br /><br />Every time I finish reading an historical novel, especially the WWII ones, I find the need to congratulate myself. It’s no secret that those novels are usually heavy in emotions and historical elements.<br /><br />Yet Ruta Sepetys made reading this YA historical novel so easy. I didn’t even feel the necessity to take a dozen breaks between chapters. And that’s because it’s so…<br /><br />Accessible. You don’t have to be a university student to understand fully what happens in this book. You don’t even need to be knowledgeable about World War II. The only thing you need to do is pay close attention to what the characters are saying.<br /><br />Which isn’t hard at all. Ruta Sepetys’ writing is simple enough that we understand absolutely everything she is saying, but not so simple that it feels as if it were written by a kindergartener. It’s actually very lyrical. <br /><br />This novel is narrated from four distinct point of views/characters – Alfred, Florian, Joana and Emilia – who are all brought together on the Wilhelm Gustloff by the catastrophic war. <br /><br />Like many people, I forgot about this terrible part of the Second World War. I first heard about this ship when I watched the movie The Imitation Game, if this is indeed the ship that was mentioned in the movie, yet I only connected the dots when things started getting awry in the novel. Even more so than they are already were. <br /><br />What a tragic event. So many lives. How did I not learn about this ship in high school? Thank you, books and movies (if that’s the ship!).<br /><br /><a href="https://hitormissbooks.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/LolaReviewer" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a>Twitter</a> | <a>Instagram</a> | <a href="https://plus.google.com/u/0/105021852309973899120/posts" rel="nofollow noopener">Google+</a> | <a href="https://www.bloglovin.com/blogs/hit-miss-books-12564715" rel="nofollow noopener">Bloglovin’</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="13295872412830525123" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1554280208" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1554280208" />
    <a title="Riley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/23179211-riley"><img alt="Riley" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1601446413p2/23179211.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1554280208?book_show_action=true">Feb 19, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Riley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Riley" href="/user/show/23179211-riley">Riley</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1554280208" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5350408674825230940">Update: Here is my video review <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=oubBCFXnq0w'>https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=oubBC...</a><br/><br/>This book is a masterpiece. It takes place during WW2 and follows 4 characters as they are seeking freedom on the Wilhelm Gustloff, a ship that promises safety to all. Going into it I was very apprehensive about reading it. Historical fiction is not a genre I typically reach for. But this book blew me away. It's safe to say that this book was the best book I have read this year. <br/><br/>The writing in the book was so phenomenal. The</span>
  <span id="freeText5350408674825230940" style="display:none">Update: Here is my video review <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=oubBCFXnq0w">https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=oubBC...</a><br /><br />This book is a masterpiece. It takes place during WW2 and follows 4 characters as they are seeking freedom on the Wilhelm Gustloff, a ship that promises safety to all. Going into it I was very apprehensive about reading it. Historical fiction is not a genre I typically reach for. But this book blew me away. It's safe to say that this book was the best book I have read this year. <br /><br />The writing in the book was so phenomenal. The way that Ruta laid out the story through her writing was so just beautiful. I felt like every single word in this novel had a purpose. There were these sentences that she would lace throughout the different points-of-view to connect them that I just thought was so brilliant. <br /><br />Out of the four main characters I loved 3 of them. I felt so much for them and their struggles. Towards the end of the book I felt like they were people I knew and I desperately wished I could change their fate. I also LOVED the side characters just as much as the main. The one main character I didn't like was a character that you aren't suppose to like so that wasn't necessarily a problem. I just didn't find myself enjoying his chapters as much as the others. <br /><br />This is a book that I know will stick with me and I am going to be thinking about these characters forever. You definitely won't want to miss this book! <br /></span>

<div id="review_1845549006" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1845549006" />
    <a title="Crumb" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/53025065-crumb"><img alt="Crumb" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1514642499p2/53025065.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1845549006?book_show_action=true">Dec 21, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Crumb" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Crumb" href="/user/show/53025065-crumb">Crumb</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/53025065-crumb?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/53025065-crumb?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1845549006" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6460676430846668822">“How foolish to believe we are more powerful than the sea or the sky.” <br/><br/><br/><b>ALL THE FEELS!</b> <br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1515250222ra/24846174.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25614492.Salt_to_the_Sea' title='Salt to the Sea by Ruta Sepetys' rel='nofollow noopener'>Salt to the Sea</a> by <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/3407448.Ruta_Sepetys' title='Ruta Sepetys' rel='nofollow noopener'>Ruta Sepetys</a> nurtured my body, it fed my soul, it made my heart soar. I also had a wave of despair and a feeling of intense longing when the book ended, coming to the unfortunate and fortunate realization that I would be experiencing a book hangover. (A phenomenon that occurs when you read something so good, you think you will never find something quite as good again)<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1518707622ra/25065860.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>This book was by no means</span>
  <span id="freeText6460676430846668822" style="display:none">“How foolish to believe we are more powerful than the sea or the sky.” <br><br><br><b>ALL THE FEELS!</b> <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1515250222ra/24846174.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25614492.Salt_to_the_Sea" title="Salt to the Sea by Ruta Sepetys" rel="nofollow noopener">Salt to the Sea</a> by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/3407448.Ruta_Sepetys" title="Ruta Sepetys" rel="nofollow noopener">Ruta Sepetys</a> nurtured my body, it fed my soul, it made my heart soar. I also had a wave of despair and a feeling of intense longing when the book ended, coming to the unfortunate and fortunate realization that I would be experiencing a book hangover. (A phenomenon that occurs when you read something so good, you think you will never find something quite as good again)<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1518707622ra/25065860.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This book was by no means a walk in the park or a box of Godiva chocolates. It is like you are on an emotional roller coaster, with upside down turns, twists, and drops. It will tear at your insides, it makes you want to cry and shriek.. "why is this happening" ?<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1518707712ra/25065875.gif" width="300" height="200" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This novel follows <b>Joana, Emilia, Florian, and Alfred</b>. They are young adults vying for a passage on the <i>Wilhelm Gustloff</i>. It takes place in the Winter of 1945 during World War II. These young adults and the passengers on board the Gustloff are hoping for freedom and safety from the war. <br>This book was inspired by the biggest maritime tragedy of all-time. When I had read the plot summary, I had initially thought.. "Hold up.. <i>The Titanic</i> or <i>The Lusitania </i> was the biggest tragedy in maritime history, wasn't it?" NO! It actually was the sinking of the <i>Wilhelm Gustloff</i>.<br>For more information on this event, please <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/MV_Wilhelm_Gustloff&gt;%20Click%20here%20&lt;/a&gt;&lt;br%20/&gt;&lt;br%20/&gt;I%20love%20books%20that%20teach%20you%20something,%20that%20help%20expand%20and%20contract%20my%20brain%20muscles,%20a%20little%20brain%20food,%20if%20you%20will.%20I'm%20a%20big%20historical%20fiction%20fan%20and%20&lt;a%20href=" title="Ruta Sepetys" rel="nofollow noopener">Ruta Sepetys</a> hit a home run with this one. I'd like to add a caveat about this book: If you are a reader (like me) who might generally shy away from young adult fiction, don't! I loved this!<br><br>In addition, I loved how the book was constructed. The chapters were very short. In fact, while I was reading, I kept thinking "Just one more chapter, Just one more chapter.." and then I noticed it was dark outside and I had finished the whole book! Gotta love those! #stayuptoolatecan'tfunctionbooks<br><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1518784092ra/25070714.gif" width="350" height="300" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br><br>This book was unexpected. It was executed skillfully and I loved how the author recreated the time period so effortlessly. It was clear that <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/3407448.Ruta_Sepetys" title="Ruta Sepetys" rel="nofollow noopener">Ruta Sepetys</a> had done extensive research on the subject matter and time period, leaving meticulous details throughout the book indicating her extensive knowledge. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/3407448.Ruta_Sepetys" title="Ruta Sepetys" rel="nofollow noopener">Ruta Sepetys</a> has a way with words that cannot be matched or duplicated. This book will leave a footprint on my heart forever, for that, I'm sure.<br><br>Highly, Highly Recommended!<br>5/5<br>Popsugar Challenge: Prompt #25 <b>A book that takes place by the sea</b><br>Buddy Read</span>
  <a data-text-id="6460676430846668822" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer16806437912637094559"><i>“Joana Vilkas, your daughter, your sister. She is salt to the sea.”</i><br/><br/>I’ve been waiting for this book ever since I finished reading <b>Between Shades of Grey</b> back in August.<br/>I’ll admit that I had very high expections for this book and I’m glad that every single one of them was met.   <span id="freeText16806437912637094559" style="display:none"><i>“Joana Vilkas, your daughter, your sister. She is salt to the sea.”</i><br><br>I’ve been waiting for this book ever since I finished reading <b>Between Shades of Grey</b> back in August.<br>I’ll admit that I had very high expections for this book and I’m glad that every single one of them was met. I could not stop reading <b>Salt to the sea</b>, I kept telling myself just one more chapter, just one more (we all know how well that works). <br><br>I enjoyed reading from every main character and <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ wished we got to read at least one chapter from Ingrid’s point of view before she died. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>I really cared for Joana and Florian, Ruta Sepetys has a special talent for powerful romances. I can’t stop thinking about them.<br>There were so many compelling moments in this book with Joana and Florian and Emilia, I had tears streaming down my face for the last 100 pages. <br><br><i>"Joana still had her mother. Reuniting with her mother was her motivation. She would slay dragons to get to her. Mother was anchor. Mother was comfort. Mother was home. ”</i><br><br>Simply put, Salt to the Sea will be added to my favorites! I loved it.<br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[THANK YOU RUTA FOR SAVING FLORIAN, BUT EMILIA- I was so sure that Emilia would reunite with her baby.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br>Also, listened to this <a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=cxjvTXo9WWM" rel="nofollow noopener">song </a> while reading, which made my reading experience a lot more emotional.<br><br>ARC from Netgalley (Thank You).<br><br><i>*Note: I'm an Amazon Affiliate. <div id="review_1641557338" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1641557338" />
    <a title="Candace" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16384209-candace"><img alt="Candace" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1459720769p2/16384209.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1641557338?book_show_action=true">Apr 01, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Candace" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Candace" href="/user/show/16384209-candace">Candace</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/25729161-salt-to-the-sea">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16384209-candace?shelf=dangerous-hero-themed-books-read">dangerous-hero-themed-books-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16384209-candace?shelf=listened-to-audio-version">listened-to-audio-version</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16384209-candace?shelf=pregnant-heroines">pregnant-heroines</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16384209-candace?shelf=historical">historical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16384209-candace?shelf=sweet-heart-warming-stories">sweet-heart-warming-stories</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1641557338" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15322303989989528611">Before starting 'Salt to the Sea', I had heard quite a lot of praise for the book. In fact, I was a little nervous to start it because I was afraid that it wouldn't live up to it's reputation. Thankfully, that didn't prove to be the case. This book was beautiful, devastatingly so.<br/><br/>Ms. Sepetys does a wonderful job of shedding light on the sinking of the Wilhelm Gustloff, a maritime disaster that claimed more than 9,000 lives and remains an overlooked part of history. Admittedly, I had never heard </span>
  <span id="freeText15322303989989528611" style="display:none">Before starting 'Salt to the Sea', I had heard quite a lot of praise for the book. In fact, I was a little nervous to start it because I was afraid that it wouldn't live up to it's reputation. Thankfully, that didn't prove to be the case. This book was beautiful, devastatingly so.<br /><br />Ms. Sepetys does a wonderful job of shedding light on the sinking of the Wilhelm Gustloff, a maritime disaster that claimed more than 9,000 lives and remains an overlooked part of history. Admittedly, I had never heard of this disaster until reading this book. Perhaps this is the result of a world that was less than sympathetic to German pain and loss following the end of WWII and the unveiling of the Nazi atrocities. Whatever the reason, I am glad that Ms. Sepetys brought this piece of history into the light. This story needed to be told.<br /><br />Weaving fact and fiction together seamlessly, the author tells the story of a group of WWII refugees trying to flee as the Russian troops gain ground toward the end of WWII. Told in alternating POVs, this book reveals a human side of war. Everybody seems to have something to hide and a different motivation for their actions. Above all else, this story highlights the fight to survive.<br /><br />Most noticeable in this cast of characters are: Joana, the Lithuanian nurse; Emilia, a young Polish girl; Florian, Emilia's mysterious rescuer; and Alfred, a young German soldier. There is a full cast of supporting characters as well, such as the shoemaker, that contribute to the richness of this story. Each play a significant role in making this a robust reading experience.<br /><br />I don't want to spoil this story for anyone. Obviously, the ship sinks. However, I won't say much else about the storyline because I think this is a story worth experiencing.<br /><br />This isn't a rainbows and unicorns type of story. It is real and moving. At times painful, this book highlights the depths of human depravity, as well as the incredible kindness that people are capable of. This is a story of tragedy and survival. It was raw, gritty and inspiring. I enjoyed this story quite a bit and would recommend it without reservations to anyone that is looking for a good, historical fiction that addresses a lesser-known part of WWII history. </span>
  <a data-text-id="15322303989989528611" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1579250277" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1579250277" />
    <a title="Dannii Elle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/44487975-dannii-elle"><img alt="Dannii Elle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1508499419p2/44487975.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1579250277?book_show_action=true">Mar 14, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dannii Elle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dannii Elle" href="/user/show/44487975-dannii-elle">Dannii Elle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780141347400" href="/book/show/28103790-salt-to-the-sea">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44487975-dannii-elle?shelf=historical-highness">historical-highness</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1579250277" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12687596417806859986"><b>First Read: August 2016, Rating: 5/5 stars<br/>Second Read: March 2020, Rating: 5/5 stars</b><br/><br/>I am an emotional wreck! This is such a wonderfully evocative and poignant recount of such a dark period in human history. Sepetys has brought history to life in amongst these pages filled with pain, grief and heartbreak of the worst possible kind - that caused by other human beings.<br/><br/>This split narration follows the lives of four young individuals and their alternate opinions and stances in the war. The year is 19</span>
  <span id="freeText12687596417806859986" style="display:none"><b>First Read: August 2016, Rating: 5/5 stars<br />Second Read: March 2020, Rating: 5/5 stars</b><br /><br />I am an emotional wreck! This is such a wonderfully evocative and poignant recount of such a dark period in human history. Sepetys has brought history to life in amongst these pages filled with pain, grief and heartbreak of the worst possible kind - that caused by other human beings.<br /><br />This split narration follows the lives of four young individuals and their alternate opinions and stances in the war. The year is 1945 and the civilians of Germany are fleeing for safety as Russia attacks and it appears that Hitler's reign will soon be overthrown. All evacuees are making for port, to board one of the ships they hope will bring them to comparative safety.<br /><br />This is such a heart-rending account of such a bleak period of human history and Sepetys spares her readers none of the agony and chaos of the time. Through the split perspectives we get not only a complete story, but differing perspectives on the war-torn land they are communally fleeing. The reader pieces the story line together as the protagonists reveal more about themselves, as their fear over their situation grows. With the tentative reveal of their individual humanity comes an empathetic insight into the harrowing tales that emerge. We get an insight into the past horror witnessed that fills the war-ravaged survivors as they attempt to hope for a brighter future. The grace these sensitive subject matters are handled with, however, belies the bleak nature of the text and beauty can be found in the alluring and exquisite writing.<br /><br />This is a brutal, yet honest and necessary, historical account that manages to remain historically accurate whilst using fictional personal histories to portray it. Stunning writing, harrowing stories and venerated characters - this is a story that will stay with me for a long time to come.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12687596417806859986" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1567177642" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1567177642" />
    <a title="Kai" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/41788524-kai"><img alt="Kai" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1573562141p2/41788524.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1567177642?book_show_action=true">Mar 02, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kai" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kai" href="/user/show/41788524-kai">Kai</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41788524-kai?shelf=2016">2016</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1567177642" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11050255472633642399"><i>“War is catastrophe. It breaks families in irretrievable pieces. But those who are gone are not necessarily lost.”</i><br/><br/>A Pole with a past. A Prussian with a mission. A Lithuanian with a secret. A German with issues. One ship. Three torpedoes.<br/><br/>Nearly one year ago I read the highly acclaimed novel <i>Between Shades of Grey</i>. Now Ruta Sepetys is back, with another historical telling set against the backdrop of World War II.<br/>Sepety's novels often talk of dark and dangerous times, with a light and comforting to</span>
  <span id="freeText11050255472633642399" style="display:none"><i>“War is catastrophe. It breaks families in irretrievable pieces. But those who are gone are not necessarily lost.”</i><br /><br />A Pole with a past. A Prussian with a mission. A Lithuanian with a secret. A German with issues. One ship. Three torpedoes.<br /><br />Nearly one year ago I read the highly acclaimed novel <i>Between Shades of Grey</i>. Now Ruta Sepetys is back, with another historical telling set against the backdrop of World War II.<br />Sepety's novels often talk of dark and dangerous times, with a light and comforting tone to it. Her writing style makes it easy to slip between the pages and take everything in. Her characters are heartwarming and relatable.<br /><br />I enjoyed <i>Salt to the Sea</i> in the same way that I did <i>Between Shades of Grey</i>: I liked writing, plot and characters, but something is always missing for me. Her stories are dramatic, cruel and most of all real, but I can never fully commit myself to the book or its characters.<br /><br />Side note with minor spoilers:<br />One thing that really bugged me was the portrayal of the Germans. Yes Hitler, the Nazis and many more people sucked and will forever and always continue to do so.<br />We had lots of "mean" Germans in the novel, but did the only German main character necessarily have to be a sociopathic, Hitler-loving ass without a single trace of character development? I would have loved to see him develop a conscience or compassion.<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Oh and it was great to find out about Lina's and Joana's connection! Two different books, two different stories but one family. I'm so happy for them!  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><a href="https://www.instagram.com/fantasticbooksandwheretofindem/" rel="nofollow noopener">Find more of my books on Instagram</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="11050255472633642399" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1537827457" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1537827457" />
    <a title="Kainat 《HUFFLEPUFF &amp; PROUD》" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14717996-kainat-hufflepuff-proud"><img alt="Kainat 《HUFFLEPUFF &amp; PROUD》" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1517124730p2/14717996.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1537827457?book_show_action=true">Feb 04, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kainat 《HUFFLEPUFF &amp; PROUD》" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kainat 《HUFFLEPUFF &amp; PROUD》" href="/user/show/14717996-kainat-hufflepuff-proud">Kainat 《HUFFLEPUFF &amp; PROUD》</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14717996-kainat-hufflepuff-proud?shelf=fav-hr">fav-hr</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1537827457" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16866714666801548208"><p>
  <i>
    <b> ⸨ Your daughter, your sister. <br/>She is salt to the sea, ⸩ </b>
  </i>
</p><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1473110266ra/20409508.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>This was my first book by Ruta Sepetys, and it won't be last. <br/>I have already bought "Between Shades of Gray", <br/>and "Out of the Easy" is on it's way. :D<br/><br/>I am obsessed with this remarkable author. <br/>She is so inspiring, and down to earth. <br/>Most importantly, she is a powerful storyteller. <br/>I loved the way this book is written. <br/>There are 4 POVs and each chapter is about 2-4 pages long. <br/>There are no unnecessary details, which i highly app</span>
  <span id="freeText16866714666801548208" style="display:none"><p>
  <i>
    <b> ⸨ Your daughter, your sister. <br>She is salt to the sea, ⸩ </b>
  </i>
</p><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1473110266ra/20409508.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This was my first book by Ruta Sepetys, and it won't be last. <br>I have already bought "Between Shades of Gray", <br>and "Out of the Easy" is on it's way. :D<br><br>I am obsessed with this remarkable author. <br>She is so inspiring, and down to earth. <br>Most importantly, she is a powerful storyteller. <br>I loved the way this book is written. <br>There are 4 POVs and each chapter is about 2-4 pages long. <br>There are no unnecessary details, which i highly appreciate. <br>Every single word drove the story forward. <br>It kept me on the edge of my seat the entire time. <br>Since the chapters are so short sometimes we get to witness same events form different POVs, i found that very satisfying. I didn't lose interest for a second. It might seem like i cry over every book, that's because the ones that don't make me feel anything aren't even worth mentioning.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1473129791ra/20412971.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>
  <u>Author's note</u>
</b>:<br><br>The sinking of the Gustloff is the largest maritime disaster, yet the world still knows nothing of it. I often wonder, will that ever change or will it remain just another secret swallowed by war?<br><br><b>
  <u>synopsys</u>
</b>:<br><br>As thousands of desperate refugees flock to the coast in the midst of a Soviet advance, four paths converge, vying for passage aboard the Wilhelm Gustloff, a ship that promises safety and freedom.<br><br>Yet not all promises can be kept.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1473129791ra/20412972.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>
  <u>Characters</u>
</b>:<br><br><i>
  <b>⸨Winter, 1945. Four teenagers. Four secrets.<br>Each one born of a different homeland; <br>each one hunted, and haunted, <br>by tragedy, lies…and war. ⸩ </b>
</i><br><br>I am just going to give a brief introduction<br>but i will not go into details. <br>That could be pretty spoilery. <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1473130833i/20413107.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1473130745i/20413104.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>
  <b> ⸨ I wanted to stay locked away from the pain and destruction. <br>I didn't want to be strong. I didn't want to be the 'smart girl'. <br>I was so very tired. I just wanted it all to be over. ⸩</b>
</i><br><br><b>Joana</b>: Ohmygod! I freaking love this girl! She is young Lithuanian nurse. She repatriated to Nazi Germany with her family to escape capture from the Soviet Russian forces. <br><br><i>
  <b> ⸨ Not a traitor to your country. <br>Much worse. A traitor to your soul.⸩ </b>
</i><br><br><b>Florian</b>: He is a Prussian apprentice, who stole something very valuable from Amber Room after he found out they were just using him for something he didn't sign up for. He had me right from his first chapter. I loved the way he was introduced. I adore his relationship with Emilia (it's not romantic), it's so cute how she calls him "the Knight" in her head. It was fun seeing Joana through his eyes. I didn't even want him anywhere near Alfred. I have much love for Florian.<br><br><i>
  <b> ⸨ I became good at pretending. <br>I became so good that after a while <br>the lines blurred between my truth and fiction. <br>And sometimes, when I did a really good job of pretending, <br>I even fooled myself. ⸩</b>
</i><br><br><b>Emilia</b>: A fifteen year old Polish girl, who got caught in the middle on this brutal war. I think she is my favorite of all four. Please keep in mind they are all carrying secrets, some more horrifying than others. Hers shocked me the most.<br> <br><i>
  <b> ⸨ Small hairs on the back of my neck lifted in warning. <br>This guy wasn’t a sailor. He was a sociopath in training. ⸩ </b>
</i><br><br><b>Alfred</b>: THIS MOTHERFUCKER! I hate him! Hate him so much. If it were any other book i might have put some effort into knowing him a little better, but not here! I was so afraid anytime he was around , or when anyone was left alone with him. He creeped the shit out of me. He is a sailor who adheres to Hitler's propaganda and thinks very highly of himself. He is delusional AF. He writes these creepy ass laters to this girl named "Hannelore", and everything he writes in them are lies. I knew there was something very wrong with him, and i was right.<br><br><br><br><br><br><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="16866714666801548208" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1569346129" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1569346129" />
    <a title="Whitney Atkinson" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14457130-whitney-atkinson"><img alt="Whitney Atkinson" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1550868411p2/14457130.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1569346129?book_show_action=true">Mar 04, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Whitney Atkinson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Whitney Atkinson" href="/user/show/14457130-whitney-atkinson">Whitney Atkinson</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14457130-whitney-atkinson?shelf=read-in-2016">read-in-2016</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1569346129" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1987837042966069650">YOWZA SHE DOES IT AGAIN<br/><br/>In both of Ruta's books, somehow my tears get saved until the moment I close the book, then everything I just read collapses down on me and it gets me choked up. I really really liked Between Shades of Grey because of its ending, and I was so excited to hear about Ruta's second book following non-German (mostly) WWII. I've mentioned before that i'm not a fan of books that are told by a handful of characters. I think they're hard to get into, can be confusing, and none of t</span>
  <span id="freeText1987837042966069650" style="display:none">YOWZA SHE DOES IT AGAIN<br /><br />In both of Ruta's books, somehow my tears get saved until the moment I close the book, then everything I just read collapses down on me and it gets me choked up. I really really liked Between Shades of Grey because of its ending, and I was so excited to hear about Ruta's second book following non-German (mostly) WWII. I've mentioned before that i'm not a fan of books that are told by a handful of characters. I think they're hard to get into, can be confusing, and none of them end up being fleshed out very well. This book is an example of one that takes 4 perspectives, but executes it very well-done. I loved all four of the characters for separate reasons. They all were four different pieces to a puzzle that had very distinct personalities and each fit a certain shape into the book's equation. Every character came from a different country and each had their own set of goals to accomplish, which made each perspective very compelling and I didn't like one voice over any of the others. Because each of their chapters was so short, this book zoomed by. That combined with the fact that every character had a secret that was one step away from being revealed, it kept me on my toes for the entire book. This book was equal parts heart-warming and tragic (though at times it lingered a bit on the horrific, but what else are you expecting in a book about genocide?). I adored every character and enjoyed how the book stayed true to the time-- not everyone got a happy ending. That conclusion, once again, was very memorable, and I would highly recommend this book if you like 20th century historical fiction.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1987837042966069650" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2571108628" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2571108628" />
    <a title="jessica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10171516-jessica"><img alt="jessica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1509983330p2/10171516.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2571108628?book_show_action=true">Oct 26, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="jessica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="jessica" href="/user/show/10171516-jessica">jessica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2571108628" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13716233919952359537">the sinking of the <i>wilhelm gustloff</i> is the deadliest disaster in maritime history, with losses dwarfing the death tolls of both the <i>titanic</i> and <i>lusitania</i> combined. and yet, most people have never heard of it. myself included. <br/><br/>if one of the greatest catastrophes ever recorded has become so forgotten, just think of all the small horrors people suffered during WWII that we will never even know about. my heart just aches them and the nightmares they lived through. which is why i will always apprecia</span>
  <span id="freeText13716233919952359537" style="display:none">the sinking of the <i>wilhelm gustloff</i> is the deadliest disaster in maritime history, with losses dwarfing the death tolls of both the <i>titanic</i> and <i>lusitania</i> combined. and yet, most people have never heard of it. myself included. <br /><br />if one of the greatest catastrophes ever recorded has become so forgotten, just think of all the small horrors people suffered during WWII that we will never even know about. my heart just aches them and the nightmares they lived through. which is why i will always appreciate stories like this, no matter how emotionally challenging they are to read. because sometimes you need that shock to really open your eyes. <br /><br />once again, ruta sepetys has created a story that so easily allows you to slip into the shoes of the main characters. even though these characters and i are separated by generations and lifetimes, i still felt so connected to them, joana especially. the writing in this is relatively easy and plain, but i think that simplicity ensures the story is unobstructed by anything that might take attention away from the importance of it, which is nice. <br /><br />and after reading both ruta sepetys novels back to back, ive come to the conclusion that she doesnt really like to end her stories. she kind of just randomly stops and then throws an epilogue in. and im not sure if that is to allow the reader to fill in the gaps about how they imagine the characters spent their lives after the war, but it makes me really sad. i think with stories as sensitive as this, a conclusion and closure is necessary. especially when you become so emotionally invested. <br /><br />regardless, this is a must read for anyone looking for a WWII novel that focuses on an a lesser known, but just as important, event that impacted the lives of many. including the reader.<br /><br /><b>↠ <i>3.5 stars</i></b></span>
  <a data-text-id="13716233919952359537" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1541727606" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1541727606" />
    <a title="Cheri" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/106692-cheri"><img alt="Cheri" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1601402708p2/106692.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1541727606?book_show_action=true">Sep 14, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cheri" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cheri" href="/user/show/106692-cheri">Cheri</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/106692-cheri?shelf=2016">2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/106692-cheri?shelf=poland">poland</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/106692-cheri?shelf=history-world-war-ii">history-world-war-ii</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1541727606" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18337520327963164736"><br/>“On September 1, 1939, Germany invaded Poland from the west. On September 17, 1939, Russia invaded Poland from the east. I remembered these dates. Two warning nations gripped Poland like girls fighting over a doll. One held the leg, the other the arm. They pulled so hard that one day, the head popped off. The Nazis sent our people to ghettos and concentration camps. The Soviets sent our people to gulags and Siberia. I was nine years old when it started. People changed. Faces shrived and sunk, li</span>
  <span id="freeText18337520327963164736" style="display:none"><br />“On September 1, 1939, Germany invaded Poland from the west. On September 17, 1939, Russia invaded Poland from the east. I remembered these dates. Two warning nations gripped Poland like girls fighting over a doll. One held the leg, the other the arm. They pulled so hard that one day, the head popped off. The Nazis sent our people to ghettos and concentration camps. The Soviets sent our people to gulags and Siberia. I was nine years old when it started. People changed. Faces shrived and sunk, like baked apples. Neighbors spoke in whispers. I watched them play their games. I observed them when they weren’t looking. I learned. But how long could I play this game? A ploy of war both outside and inside. What would happen if I actually made it to the West? Would I be able to reveal myself as Emilia Stożek, a girl from Lwów? Would Germany be safe for me? Once the war ended, which side would be the right side for a Pole?”<br /><br />I’ve been looking forward to reading “Salt to the Sea” since I closed the pages on “Between Shades of Gray.” Sepetys gift for sharing the stories of these moments in history we rarely learned about, told through eyes that prefer to see only seen the good in this world. Until, until life forces them to see otherwise, but their hearts still look for that goodness in the eyes of others.<br /><br />The winter of 1945 was a long and treacherous winter for these souls who had left their homes and were on a long and arduous journey, on foot, ultimately to board the Wilhelm Gustloff. To evacuate their home. <br /><br />“Germany was finally telling people what they should have said months ago. Run for your lives.”<br /><br />They did not begin their journey together, but found each other along the way, the days and nights of walking through snow and mud and freezing conditions. <br /><br />“What a group we were. A pregnant girl in love, a kindly shoemaker, an orphan boy, a blind girl, and a giantess who complained that everyone was in her way when she herself took up the most room. And me, a lonely girl who missed her family and begged for a second chance.”<br /><br />Written in short, alternating chapters, sharing the four points of view of Joana, Florian, Emilia and Alfred. Joana is a caring woman, a nurse, and older than Emilia who seems to be still in her teens. Emilia is scared; needing a mother figure to replace the mother she lost as a child, and is rescued by Florian early on. Emilia needs both her knight and her nurse. Joana dreams of a reunion with her mother. <br /><br />“No one wanted to fall into the hands of the enemy. But it was growing harder to distinguish who the enemy was.”<br /><br />Alfred is a socially awkward and disturbed German officer. “This was the type of man who looked at a picture on the wall and instead of admiring the photo, looked at his own reflection in the glass.”<br />Among the other characters you will come to know and care for are the young wandering boy and the Shoemaker, or the “shoe poet”.<br /><br />“’The shoes always tell the story,’ said the shoe poet. ‘Not always,’ I countered. ‘Yes, always. Your boots, they are expensive, well made. That tells me that you come from a wealthy family. But the style is one made for an older woman. That tells me they probably belonged to your mother. A mother sacrificed her boots for her daughter. That tells me you are loved, my dear. And your mother is not here, so that tells me that you are sad, my dear. The shoes tell the story.”<br /><br />As they come together and journey together, you begin to learn their secrets, their stories. Their journey leads them to the ship, the Wilhelm Gustloff, which will ultimately become the largest maritime disaster in history. On 30 January 1945, four torpedoes were pointed at the Wilhelm Gustloff from a Soviet submarine S-13. “Each torpedo was painted with a scrawled dedication: For the Motherland. For the Soviet People. For Leningrad. For Stalin.” Three of those torpedoes struck the Gustloff, one torpedo, “For Stalin,” did not launch.<br /><br />Approximately 10,000 people were aboard; most were civilians, including around 5,000 children. Approximately 1,000 survived. <br /><br />The largest maritime disaster in history.<br /><br />That winter, several other ships ended up in the Baltic Sea, with approximately 25,000 lives were lost in all. <br /><br />What was not lost is hope. The belief that humanity can rise up again and begin once more to unite in acceptance that despite our differences, that love will win. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="18337520327963164736" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1833299562" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1833299562" />
    <a title="Norma" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/41400192-norma"><img alt="Norma" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589038160p2/41400192.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1833299562?book_show_action=true">Jan 26, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Norma" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Norma" href="/user/show/41400192-norma">Norma</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1833299562" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13133298715128706231">Well that was enlightening, emotional, and a page-turning read!<br/><br/>SALT TO THE SEA by RUTA SEPETYS is a Historical Fiction novel that is engaging, heart-wrenching, and a powerful read with an extremely interesting plot that grabbed my attention from the very first chapter. This was definitely another page-turner and extremely hard to put down.<br/><br/>The last few books that I have read lately have either had an embossed dustjacket or cover and this is no exception as this one has a partially embossed dustja</span>
  <span id="freeText13133298715128706231" style="display:none">Well that was enlightening, emotional, and a page-turning read!<br /><br />SALT TO THE SEA by RUTA SEPETYS is a Historical Fiction novel that is engaging, heart-wrenching, and a powerful read with an extremely interesting plot that grabbed my attention from the very first chapter. This was definitely another page-turner and extremely hard to put down.<br /><br />The last few books that I have read lately have either had an embossed dustjacket or cover and this is no exception as this one has a partially embossed dustjacket as well as an embossed Stork on the actual cover. Must be some kind of theme for my reads lately! THE COVER definitely depicts an ominous read which I found extremely fitting for this novel.<br /><br />The details of the ship, Wilhelm Gustloff is a shockingly little-known piece of history from World War II that I am sad to say that I never knew anything about until after reading this author's work of historical fiction.<br /><br />Winter, 1945. Four teenagers. Four Secrets. <br /><br />SALT TO THE SEA has us following along the tale of four captivating CHARACTERS; Joana (The Nurse), Florian (The Knight), Emilia (The Polish Girl), and Alfred (The Letter Writer). I really enjoyed the format of this novel which was written in very short chapters with alternating points of view of the four characters and made me want to read "just one more chapter". I really liked what each of these characters brought to this story as well as the secondary ones throughout this book. RUTA SEPETYS delivers an unforgettable story here that was easy to follow along with the storyline and all the characters involved.<br /><br />To sum it all up it was a well researched, heartbreaking, enjoyable, quick and a fast-paced read with a satisfying ending. Would recommend!!<br /><br />Review written and posted on our themed book blog Two Sisters Lost In A Coulee Reading.<br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://twosisterslostinacoulee.com">https://twosisterslostinacoulee.com</a><br /><br />Coulee: a term applied rather loosely to different landforms, all of which refer to a kind of valley.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13133298715128706231" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1528971561" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1528971561" />
    <a title="Malia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5953660-malia"><img alt="Malia" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1476920229p2/5953660.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1528971561?book_show_action=true">Dec 28, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Malia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Malia" href="/user/show/5953660-malia">Malia</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5953660-malia?shelf=best-of-2016">best-of-2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5953660-malia?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5953660-malia?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5953660-malia?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1528971561" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16523395836423620363">This book crushed me! Despite having read and learned so much about this terrible time in our world history, I am amazed that there are constantly new aspects of it I didn't know before and which continue to stun and sadden me. Salt to the Sea, in particular touched me, because it mirrored, to a degree, what my grandmother and her family experienced. My grandmother, her little brother, her widowed mother and aunt had to flee from Silesia to escape the Russians, which is similar to why the charac</span>
  <span id="freeText16523395836423620363" style="display:none">This book crushed me! Despite having read and learned so much about this terrible time in our world history, I am amazed that there are constantly new aspects of it I didn't know before and which continue to stun and sadden me. Salt to the Sea, in particular touched me, because it mirrored, to a degree, what my grandmother and her family experienced. My grandmother, her little brother, her widowed mother and aunt had to flee from Silesia to escape the Russians, which is similar to why the characters in this book are moving west. Where the figures in this novel are headed toward the sea and the large ships to transport them to Kiel in Northern Germany, my grandmother and her family took another route, so I was not very familiar with this method of navigating the Baltic Sea at the time and the tremendous losses of life that occurred as a result of violence, negligence and desperation. It also made me think of the refugees trying to get across the Mediterranean Sea in recent times, and the incredible losses and hardships they have suffered.<br />Sepetys' method of telling the story from four points of view was beautifully done and effective in showing different motivations and mind sets at this impossible time. I don't want to give away anything, but throughout the book, I really had to stop myself from googling what really happened, even though I knew it was building up to something tragic. I was so attached to some of the characters, I almost didn't want the book to end, fearing what might happen. <br />This story was heartbreaking, and if you're looking for an easy read, this is not for you. Still, I would recommend everyone read it at some point. It tells a story that is not as public as it should be, and for the sake of remembering and honoring those who fell victim to the misery and cruelty of this war, we need to learn as much as we can so that nothing like this will happen again.<br />As I write this, I am particularly saddened by the recent slew of tragedies and acts of violence that have occurred all over the globe. A book like Salt to the Sea and countless others teach us that unity and compassion are the most important elements of being human, and the danger when those aspects are lost can change the world for the worse and set humanity back centuries.<br /><br />Find more reviews and bookish fun at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.princessandpen.com">http://www.princessandpen.com</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="16523395836423620363" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
