<div id="review_1538039679" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1538039679" />
    <a title="Aestas Book Blog" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5604583-aestas-book-blog"><img alt="Aestas Book Blog" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1353371225p2/5604583.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1538039679?book_show_action=true">Feb 04, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aestas Book Blog" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aestas Book Blog" href="/user/show/5604583-aestas-book-blog">Aestas Book Blog</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5604583-aestas-book-blog?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1538039679" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer199886113000652843"><b> ::: FULL REVIEW NOW POSTED ::: 4.5 stars</b><br/><img width='100%' src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1454728116i/18005430.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>WOAH. What an incredible book! It was vastly different than the usual books I read. I'm usually a pretty hardcore Romance genre reader, but this story swept me away! I read it in a single day and had tears in my eyes in the end (letters always make me cry) and I keep thinking about this story in the back of my mind. I just can't let go.<br/><br/>Whenever I'm going through a major book hangover, I like to try and switch up the genre I read. Given my intense love of </span>
  <span id="freeText199886113000652843" style="display:none"><b> ::: FULL REVIEW NOW POSTED ::: 4.5 stars</b><br><img width="100%" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1454728116i/18005430.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>WOAH. What an incredible book! It was vastly different than the usual books I read. I'm usually a pretty hardcore Romance genre reader, but this story swept me away! I read it in a single day and had tears in my eyes in the end (letters always make me cry) and I keep thinking about this story in the back of my mind. I just can't let go.<br><br>Whenever I'm going through a major book hangover, I like to try and switch up the genre I read. Given my intense love of reading, doing this allows me to still read, while trying something new, and yet allowing my emotions from my previous book the time to settle. So this time, I tried this book. Even though it's not the kind of book I'd usually read, something about the cover, the title, and blurb really grabbed my attention.<br><br>The writing was absolutely incredible. Flawless and profound. This author is a very gifted storyteller. But her method in this book was unlike anything else I’ve ever read. Each chapter was literally only 1-3 pages long (!!) and each chapter was told from the points of view of four of the main characters (it switched each time). While it was weird at first, I caught on quickly to the rhythm and found that it totally worked for this story. In fact, I found it was astonishingly effective at portraying such a large-scale story as this, one that had so many different storylines converging in on each other, in a manner that made it completely character-driven. I genuinely loved it. The YA Historical Romance genre is nowhere near what I usually read, but I’m so glad I decided to read this particular one! It was powerful and beautifully written.<br><br><blockquote>
  <strong>
    <em>Winter, 1945. Four teenagers. Four secrets.<br></em>
  </strong>
  <br>
  <br>
  <strong>
    <em>Each one born of a different homeland; each one hunted, and haunted, by tragedy, lies…and war. </em>
  </strong>
  <br>
  <br>
  <strong>
    <em>As thousands of desperate refugees flock to the coast in the midst of a Soviet advance, four paths converge, vying for passage aboard the Wilhelm Gustloff, a ship that promises safety and freedom. </em>
  </strong>
  <br>
  <br>
  <strong>
    <em>Yet not all promises can be kept.</em>
  </strong>
  <br>
  <br>
  <strong>
    <em>Inspired by the single greatest tragedy in maritime history, this bestselling and award-winning author lifts the veil on a shockingly little-known casualty of World War II. An illuminating and life-affirming tale of heart and hope.</em>
  </strong>
</blockquote><br>The story begins with all these different characters, for different reasons, all trying to make their way to docks, where they hope to board a ship that will take them to safety. But in order to get there, they first had to survive a dangerous journey on land through enemy check points, under fire from all sides, in danger of becoming victims of the brutal winter, in the middle of one of the largest wars in history.<br><br>A nurse.<br>A blind girl.<br>A shoemaker.<br>A mysterious soldier.<br>A pregnant teen.<br>A delusional sociopath.<br>A wandering boy.<br>A devastating war.<br>A bitter winer.<br>Thousands of miles.<br>One ill-fated sea voyage.<br><br>The chapters are all very short like I mentioned but every single one of them packs a <em>punch </em>and ends strong -- which is really a testament to the power of this author's writing. The upside to this storytelling method too is that there is no fluff in the book at all. You're told everything you need to know and nothing more. Everything has meaning. And everything drives the story forward.<br><br>Things get quite intense the more you read, especially when the different storylines begin to converge. It's like, you desperately want them all to stay together, and you naturally want them to get to safety and even though you know the ship is doomed, a part of you can't help but hope that it isn't. So it's like counter-intuitive. You should be wanting all their plans to fall apart so that they can be safe. It's such an interesting internal conflict to go through as a reader because you naturally want to root for their plans to work out.<br><br>Now, not to belittle the value of even one human life, but I just want to put some things into perspective for you to give you a sense of scale. The <em>Titanic</em> (which is widely known as one of the most famously tragic maritime disasters), lost 1,503 passengers when it went down. The <em>Wilhelm Gustloff</em> was built to carry 1,463 people. On the day it was sunk, it was carrying 10,574. It is estimated that 9,400 people died. The <em>Titanic</em> took two hours and forty minutes to sink. The <em>Wilhelm Gustloff</em> took less than an hour.<br><br><blockquote>
  <em>How foolish to believe we are more powerful than the sea or the sky.</em>
</blockquote><br>When the torpedos hit, <em>my heart was racing</em>. I'd just spent a huge chunk of this book getting invested in these characters lives. Characters who I knew wouldn't all be able to make it. It was beyond intense.<br><br>Also, while this is absolutely not a Romance at all, there is actually a little bit of a romance within one of the storylines, and I'm just going to come out and tell you that that romance does get a HEA. I don't want you to think this is a book where everyone just dies in the end. That's not the case. There is a lot of loss. But ultimately, this is both a story of loss and survival.<br><br>The ending left me with tears in my eyes. Letters always make me cry in book. And I was so surprised that my reaction at the very end was a smile on my face despite the tears... Like I said, this genre is not one I usually read or recommend from, but this particular book stood out to me and made me want to read it. If you're in the mood to read something different, or maybe if this is a genre you already love, give this a try!<br><br><blockquote>
  <em>
    <strong>The sinking of the Gustloff is the largest maritime disaster, yet the world still knows nothing of it. I often wonder, will that ever change or will it remain just another secret swallowed by war?</strong>
  </em>
</blockquote><br><br>The final thing I want to leave you with is a quote from the author's note at the back of the book...<br><blockquote>
  <em>Every nation has hidden history, countless stories preserved only by those who experienced them. Stories of war are often read and discussed worldwide by readers whose nations stood on opposite sides during battle. History divided us, but through reading we can be united in story, study, and remembrance. Books join us together as a global reading community, but more important, a global human community striving to learn from the past.</em>
  <br>
  <br>
  <em>What determines how we remember history and which elements are preserved and penetrate the collective consciousness? If historical novels stir your interest, pursue the facts, the history, memoirs, and personal testimonies available. These are the shoulders that historical fiction sits upon. When the survivors are gone we must not let the truth disappear with them.</em>
  <br>
  <br>
  <em>Please, give them a voice.</em>
</blockquote><br><strong>Rating: 4.5 stars. Standalone YA Historical Fiction.</strong><br>__________________________<br><br><b> For more of my reviews, book news and updates:<br>✦ <a href="http://aestasbookblog.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Main blog: Aestas Book Blog</a><br>✦ <a href="http://www.facebook.com/pages/Aestas-Book-Blog/332404836826905" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook Blog Page</a><br>✦ <a href="https://twitter.com/AestasBookBlog" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> <br>✦ <a href="http://aestasbookblog.com/subscribe/" rel="nofollow noopener">Subscribe by email</a> <br><br><a href="http://aestasbookblog.com" rel="nofollow noopener"><img width="100%" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380306821i/688100._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a> </b></span>
  <a data-text-id="199886113000652843" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_2698658327" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2698658327" />
    <a title="Zainab" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/48759239-zainab"><img alt="Zainab" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1600887871p2/48759239.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2698658327?book_show_action=true">Feb 10, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Zainab" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Zainab" href="/user/show/48759239-zainab">Zainab</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2085485566" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer4915539076224624828">1.5⭐️<br/><br/>NO. JUST. NO. <br/>Absolutely infuriating. <br/><br/>✨ <b> Expectations vs. reality:</b><br/><br/>Misleading synopsis. <br/>I expected a book that recounted the worst maritime tragedy in recorded history. I got... well, let’s not. <br/><br/>This was supposed to be about the Wilhelm Gustloff, a German military transport ship which was sunk in 1945 by the soviets in the Baltic Sea and one that cost in estimate, 9,400 lives, making it the largest maritime disaster in history.<br/><br/>And though I have no problem with character-driven books (actuall</span>
  <span id="freeText4915539076224624828" style="display:none">1.5⭐️<br /><br />NO. JUST. NO. <br />Absolutely infuriating. <br /><br />✨ <b> Expectations vs. reality:</b><br /><br />Misleading synopsis. <br />I expected a book that recounted the worst maritime tragedy in recorded history. I got... well, let’s not. <br /><br />This was supposed to be about the Wilhelm Gustloff, a German military transport ship which was sunk in 1945 by the soviets in the Baltic Sea and one that cost in estimate, 9,400 lives, making it the largest maritime disaster in history.<br /><br />And though I have no problem with character-driven books (actually, I love it), IT DID NOT WORK HERE because it detracted from the actual main point of the book. <br /><b>This was basically about four teenagers whose lives converge during the course of the book rather than the tragedy that took place. <br />It had NOTHING to do with the ship or the sinking of the ship, the characters just happened to be on it and that’s about it.</b><br /><br /></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1409801378" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9317293503892313974">Sepetys does it again with this "sequel" to Between Shades of Grey. Another heart-wrenching tale of WWII involving not very well known Russian/German conflicts and the innocent people affected by them.<br/><br/>If you are a fan of historical fiction, WWII fiction, or using up a couple boxes of tissues because of a good tear-jerker, this is a great book to check out.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText15556752184045202879" style="display:none">""A momentary quiet followed, leaving nothing but the sound of the wind and waves. We bobbed up<br />and back, up and back, waves lapping and curling, the sound of crying filtering through the dark."" <br /><br /><br />Intense and Glorified writing and character.<br />Exceptional narration.<br />My favorite character- Shoemaker<br />"“I wept because i had no shoes, <br />until i met a man who had no feet.” <br /><br />"That is class of writing when reader thinks whether the story is fiction or reality, Just like story line of movie- THE WORDS."<br /> Historical reader, Highly recommended one !<br />Contented and Superfluous Fiction about WWII time span, It reveals all the circumstances and possessions made by Stalin and Hitler and the different community's person got affected in their own and worthwhile manner.<br /><br />Few lines I loved -<br />*"I had the knight’s pack.<br />The knight had the baby.<br />The knight would want his pack.<br />I wanted my baby"<br />*"There’s a saying, ‘Death hath a thousand doors to let out life; I shall find<br />one"<br />*"I knew the legends of the birds. Seagulls were the souls of dead soldiers. Owls were the souls of<br />women. Doves were the recently departed souls of unmarried girls.<br />Was there a bird for the souls of people like me?"<br /><br /> *"Yes, always. Your boots, they are expensive, well made. That tells me that you come from a<br />wealthy family. But the style is one made for an older woman. That tells me they probably belonged<br />to your mother. A mother sacrificed her boots for her daughter. That tells me you are loved, my dear.<br />And your mother is not here, so that tells me that you are sad, my dear. The shoes tell the story."</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('QOELByLwLtiYEL06RVj4p5Zrm/2c2m2bBJQTUDZHlsh6x2LVma7nsD87CVuyrfJ4QDR8NVJX4/xf6lXh+wRkUg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('dgF9O81bVlg7jXrl1JMzE0wH0yYUqhKOpF8jIXfHc75MJxTpdgWfMJymzoQjZjnMmlg07tonnOn/IWWQuoSBJA==')})
  }

She doesn’t believe that the Nazis will invade France…but invade they do, in droves of marching soldiers, in caravans of trucks and tanks, in planes that fill the skies and drop bombs upon the innocent. When a German captain requisitions Vianne’s home, she and her daughter must live with the enemy or lose everything. Without food or money or hope, as danger escalates all around them, she is forced to make one impossible choice after another to keep her family alive.\n\nVianne’s sister, Isabelle, is a rebellious eighteen-year-old, searching for purpose with all the reckless passion of youth. While thousands of Parisians march into the unknown terrors of war, she meets Gaëtan, a partisan who believes the French can fight the Nazis from within France, and she falls in love as only the young can…completely. But when he betrays her, Isabelle joins the Resistance and never looks back, risking her life time and again to save others.\n\nWith courage, grace and powerful insight, bestselling author Kristin Hannah captures the epic panorama of World War II and illuminates an intimate part of history seldom seen: the women’s war. The Nightingale tells the stories of two sisters, separated by years and experience, by ideals, passion and circumstance, each embarking on her own dangerous path toward survival, love, and freedom in German-occupied, war-torn France—a heartbreakingly beautiful novel that celebrates the resilience of the human spirit and the durability of women. <span id="freeTextContainer1310439699611495338"><b>#1 New York Times Bestselling Author and Winner of the Carnegie Medal.</b><br/>Ruta Sepetys was born and raised in Michigan in a family of artists, readers, and music lovers. The daughter of a refugee, Ruta is drawn to underrepresented stories of strength through struggle and hopes to give voice to those who weren't able to tell their story. Her award-winning historical novels are published in over fifty c</span>
  <span id="freeText1310439699611495338" style="display:none"><b>#1 New York Times Bestselling Author and Winner of the Carnegie Medal.</b><br />Ruta Sepetys was born and raised in Michigan in a family of artists, readers, and music lovers. The daughter of a refugee, Ruta is drawn to underrepresented stories of strength through struggle and hopes to give voice to those who weren't able to tell their story. Her award-winning historical novels are published in over fifty countries and have received over forty literary prizes.<br /><br />For more information:<br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.rutasepetys.com">https://www.rutasepetys.com</a><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.facebook.com/rutasepetys">https://www.facebook.com/rutasepetys</a><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.instagram.com/rutasepetysauthor">https://www.instagram.com/rutasepetys...</a><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.twitter.com/rutasepetys">https://www.twitter.com/rutasepetys</a><br /></span>
